<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_74798a40-2566-4138-94da-38655933513a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer11687701934033180888">This is an accurate portrayal of me after reading The Assassin's Curse:<br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/506877.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In fact. You know, what? Hit it:<br/><br/>Ananna is a pirate, born and raised <br/>and on the high seas is where she spends her days. <br/>Sword fightin', riggin', stealing your loot. <br/>Handy with a lie and a knife in her boot. <br/>All she wants is to travel to distant lands, <br/>but her mom and pop are plotting marriage plans.<br/>She'll take adventure over a relationship, <br/>so on the big day gives her fiance the slip.<br/>She has no idea just what trouble she's in</span>
  <span id="freeText11687701934033180888" style="display:none">This is an accurate portrayal of me after reading The Assassin's Curse:<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/506877.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In fact. You know, what? Hit it:<br><br>Ananna is a pirate, born and raised <br>and on the high seas is where she spends her days. <br>Sword fightin', riggin', stealing your loot. <br>Handy with a lie and a knife in her boot. <br>All she wants is to travel to distant lands, <br>but her mom and pop are plotting marriage plans.<br>She'll take adventure over a relationship, <br>so on the big day gives her fiance the slip.<br>She has no idea just what trouble she's in, <br>turns out he wasn't joking about that assassin.<br><br>Naji's an assassin with a capital A. <br>He's got a new target, he's stalking his prey.<br>He's the shadow behind her in the dead of night, <br>knows eighty ways to kill, never lost a fight.<br>All covered in blood magic, scars and tattoos. <br>He'll meet her in the desert for a midnight duel.<br>But versus Ananna, he experiences a first: <br>instead of an easy kill they both get cursed.<br>Enemies become allies if only to survive. <br>The Curse is Impossible but they still have to try... <br><br>Dance Break!<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393761ra/758192.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><s>I'm sorry.</s> I'm not sorry. This book was so much fun!<br><br>There are few things I like better than reading about two adversaries forced to become allies in pursuit of some higher goal. When Ananna accidentally triggers a curse binding herself with her would-be assassin, Naji, they quickly become one of my most favorite Buddy Cops of Convenience of all time. The awkward teamwork! The reluctant bonding! The coordinated sword fights! Your ideas are intriguing to me and I wish to subscribe to your newsletter!<br><br>What makes this particular team so perfect is that both sides of the partnership hold equal weight. You'd think that might be hard to pull off with one side being a legendary blood magic assassin and all, but Ananna is no wilting flower either. In fact one of the most enjoyable parts of the book for me was how often Ananna nonchalantly saved Naji's ass. Perfect heroine is perfect. Etc. Etc.<br><br>As much as I enjoyed this first book, I can already tell the sequel is going to be even better. I cannot wait to get my greedy hands on it. As is, though, The Assassin's Curse is a gem and has the perfect blend of hijinks and high stakes.<br><br>Rating: 4/5 stars.<br><br><b>Warning:</b> I bought the paperback and the back cover copy includes developments that happen within the last 10 pages or so of the book so just go ahead and stick with the Goodreads summary if you don't want to know the set up for the next book until you get there. <br><br><i>This review originally appeared on <a href="http://youngadultanonymous.blogspot.com/2012/10/review-assassins-curse-by-cassandra.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Young Adult Anonymous</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11687701934033180888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1439112299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1439112299" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1439112299?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1439112299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6504114587553151337">2 1/2 stars. So, I finally tried the much-recommended <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13533650.The_Assassin_s_Curse__The_Assassin_s_Curse___1_' title='The Assassin's Curse (The Assassin's Curse, #1) by Cassandra Rose Clarke' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Assassin's Curse</a> after all this time. I recently tried Clarke's adult novel - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22907961.Our_Lady_of_the_Ice' title='Our Lady of the Ice by Cassandra Rose Clarke' rel='nofollow noopener'>Our Lady of the Ice</a> - and found it painfully slow, but I wanted to see how her YA book compared. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13533650.The_Assassin_s_Curse__The_Assassin_s_Curse___1_' title='The Assassin's Curse (The Assassin's Curse, #1) by Cassandra Rose Clarke' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Assassin's Curse</a> was not as slow as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22907961.Our_Lady_of_the_Ice' title='Our Lady of the Ice by Cassandra Rose Clarke' rel='nofollow noopener'>Our Lady of the Ice</a> and I was able to finish it, however, I am a little surprised by all the hype. There were some parts that I had to push myself through and I can say I have no desire to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15714476.The_Pirate_s_Wish__The_Assassin_s_Curse___2_' title='The Pirate's Wish (The Assassin's Curse, #2) by Cassandra Rose Clarke' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Pirate's Wish</a>.<br/><br/>Firstly, there </span>
  <span id="freeText6504114587553151337" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. So, I finally tried the much-recommended <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13533650.The_Assassin_s_Curse__The_Assassin_s_Curse___1_" title="The Assassin's Curse (The Assassin's Curse, #1) by Cassandra Rose Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">The Assassin's Curse</a> after all this time. I recently tried Clarke's adult novel - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22907961.Our_Lady_of_the_Ice" title="Our Lady of the Ice by Cassandra Rose Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">Our Lady of the Ice</a> - and found it painfully slow, but I wanted to see how her YA book compared. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13533650.The_Assassin_s_Curse__The_Assassin_s_Curse___1_" title="The Assassin's Curse (The Assassin's Curse, #1) by Cassandra Rose Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">The Assassin's Curse</a> was not as slow as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22907961.Our_Lady_of_the_Ice" title="Our Lady of the Ice by Cassandra Rose Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">Our Lady of the Ice</a> and I was able to finish it, however, I am a little surprised by all the hype. There were some parts that I had to push myself through and I can say I have no desire to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15714476.The_Pirate_s_Wish__The_Assassin_s_Curse___2_" title="The Pirate's Wish (The Assassin's Curse, #2) by Cassandra Rose Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pirate's Wish</a>.<br /><br />Firstly, there is <b>no world-building</b>. Occasionally, I can forgive this when the scope of the novel is small. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13549218.Death_Sworn__Death_Sworn___1_" title="Death Sworn (Death Sworn, #1) by Leah Cypess" rel="nofollow noopener">Death Sworn</a>, which takes place within a cave. However, this book moves from the seas, through towns, through desert and swamp, back to the seas and to the dark "Isles of the Sky" and I have no idea what's going on in this world at all. <br /><br />I've learned nothing about the system of magic, nothing about the laws and ruling system, very little about the geography, very little about the pirates and their ways/customs... very little about anybody or anything.<br /><br />The story begins with Ananna running away from her parents and her life as a pirate to avoid marrying into another pirate clan. This is a very emotionless undertaking - how does Ananna feel about leaving her parents? How does she feel about their desire to marry her off? Because, honestly, she seems unaffected. She simply runs away.<br /><br />The pirate clan then decide to send an assassin after her. But, in a bizarre twist of fate, Ananna accidentally saves the assassin's life and triggers a curse - one which forces the assassin (Naji) to become Ananna's protector. Neither of them is particularly happy about this, so they set out to break the curse.<br /><br />I'm starting to realize that I am <b>not fond of journey books</b>. The kind where the major plot points happen at the start and end of the book and the in between is one long-ass journey between the two. I think it also weakened <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17564519.Walk_on_Earth_a_Stranger__The_Gold_Seer___1_" title="Walk on Earth a Stranger (The Gold Seer, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">Walk on Earth a Stranger</a>, though it weakened this book more. <br /><br />The long journey between triggering the curse and getting to the person who can help them find a cure is <b>so slow</b>. Of course, it's peppered with random bits of action, fights and chases, but it all <b>feels like filler</b> to pad out the book. I had to force myself not to skim read. <br /><br />Also, I think this type of plot structure *might* work better if the characters were more interesting and had more chemistry. Not necessarily romantic chemistry, but at least some spark of something between them, because pretty much the whole book is made up of interactions between Ananna and Naji, and damn, they are so dull together.<br /><br />Ananna is more likable if you enjoy cardboard cutout "strong heroines", but Naji is just cold and boring. I never felt any emotion for him.<br /><br />Clearly, Clarke is just not an author for me, but I am glad I finally checked this out for myself. I do wonder if I would have enjoyed this book three years ago when it was first released; back when strong heroines and broody assassins were not quite so overdone and would have been right up my alley. Oh well.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6504114587553151337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1949752625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1949752625" />
    <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews"><img alt="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492999740p2/66199133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1949752625?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews">Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=reviews-of-the-year">reviews-of-the-year</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=pirates">pirates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=favorite-heroine">favorite-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=random-shit">random-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=quiet-alpha-males">quiet-alpha-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=assassin">assassin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=magic-etc">magic-etc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1949752625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17165567058470813295">There are few things <b>I FUCKING LOVE MORE</b> than reading about two adversaries <b>FORCED to become allies</b> for some higher goal. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455898999ra/18166677.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Saving the assassin <b>Nanji</b>'s life binds him and <b>Ananna</b> together so Naji HAS TO protect her. <u><b>The awkward teamwork! The reluctant bonding!</b> Yelling at each other while fighting people!</u> An odd pair but they were great<br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>”Well, look who’s on my front porch,” he said, speaking Empire with this odd hissing accent. “A murderer and a cross-dressing pirate.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/> I know i've emphasi</span>
  <span id="freeText17165567058470813295" style="display:none">There are few things <b>I FUCKING LOVE MORE</b> than reading about two adversaries <b>FORCED to become allies</b> for some higher goal. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455898999ra/18166677.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Saving the assassin <b>Nanji</b>'s life binds him and <b>Ananna</b> together so Naji HAS TO protect her. <u><b>The awkward teamwork! The reluctant bonding!</b> Yelling at each other while fighting people!</u> An odd pair but they were great<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>”Well, look who’s on my front porch,” he said, speaking Empire with this odd hissing accent. “A murderer and a cross-dressing pirate.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br> I know i've emphasized my taste for independent and courageous heroines<br>So here's my reaction when I read the summary: <b>a freaking PIRATE heroine? A curse? Several impossible tasks with an underlying Arabic mythology? An ASSASSIN who wants to kill her?</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451390225ra/17537204.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440615964ra/15999873.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Both characters are equally KICKASS ~one being a legendary blood magic assassin while the other is an adventurous sword-fighting pirate princess!<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You know, that pissed me off. We'd traveled half around the world to get to him, and there were monsters chasing us and Naji's curse was impossible to break, and here he was cracking jokes about our professions.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> So, as you may have noticed, with her humor and her knife, Ananna won a place in my favorite heroines OF ALL TIMESSSS<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455435637ra/18100723.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She was so feisty and felt so real. She knew how to fight, rule a ship, and basic survival stuff like construct shelters. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Um... I'm sorry?" I waited for a few minutes, watching him. Then I asked, "Are you going to kill me or what?"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> Then Naji the famous assassin- Mysterious, reckless, <u>kinda grumpy</u>, and attitude of an actual assassin (not some sissy-pretender). The moment he sat down, sullenly complaining about Ananna saving his life I loved him<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"She moved like water, graceful and soft and lovely. Every part of me wanted to stick out my foot and trip her, just to see her stumble.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451952649ra/17625493.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now the cons...... *frowny face*<br>For a book that travels across seas, towns, deserts, swamps, then a mystical "Isles of the Sky" you'd think the author would explain what the heck is happening in the world.<br><br>So theres some <u>magic</u> but <b>you don't know anything about the magic. </b><br>Theres <u>villages and cities</u> but <b>nothing about the laws</b> and ruling system. <br>Our main character is a pirate and the <u>entirety of the pirate's ways</u> &amp; traditions were summarized into a single sentence: <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"There are three ways of bettering yourself in the Pirates' Confederation, Mama told me once: murder, mutiny, and marriage."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489864888ra/22258197.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thats nice and all BUT HOW ABOUT SOME WORLD BUILDING! <br><br>It literally starts with Ananna running away. It was THE MOST <b>emotionless scene I have ever read</b>. How does Ananna feel about leaving her parents? Their desire to just marry her off for a "pirate alliance"? <b>Nothing.</b> She simply runs away. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493844542ra/22658612.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But thats not okay so the ditched fiancé pirate sends an <b>assassin</b> after her...? This is where the book picks up because in a bizarre twist she ends up saving the assassin's life<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490535170ra/22321802.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>”Two weeks in the desert all on account of some assassin who doesn’t know how to look out for snakes.”<br>“If you hadn’t killed that snake,” Naji said calmly, “I would have killed you.”<br>“Oh, shut up.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Great characters, decent action-pace, and the world seemed interesting~ I just wanted to learn more about it. Expectations for book two rising.<b> Highly Recommend </b><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465455196ra/19357126.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_351824654" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351824654" />
    <a title="Zuleeza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4883387-zuleeza"><img alt="Zuleeza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392172290p2/4883387.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351824654?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zuleeza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zuleeza" href="/user/show/4883387-zuleeza">Zuleeza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4883387-zuleeza?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4883387-zuleeza?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351824654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16269258769958596037">This review is also available on my blog, <a href='http://zue-leysza.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Qwerty</a><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380381327ra/738556.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Easily, the BEST BOOK of 2012 I've read so far.<br/><br/>First, I would like to offer a shitload of virtual Nutella for mah girls, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3068554-ebony' rel='nofollow noopener'><br/>Ebony</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8282085-lisbeth-domus-libri-avery' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lisbeth</a> as a sign of gratitute. Without their gushing reviews, I wouldn't go about requesting this from Netgalley.<br/><br/>I think I may have found my favourite book of 2012 so far.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381327i/738557.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>No, I'm not kitten you. <br/><br/>My favourite shelf had been so loneleyh! SO LONELEYH! No books, and I mean no books had ever made it into that list after Da</span>
  <span id="freeText16269258769958596037" style="display:none">This review is also available on my blog, <a href="http://zue-leysza.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Qwerty</a><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380381327ra/738556.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Easily, the BEST BOOK of 2012 I've read so far.<br><br>First, I would like to offer a shitload of virtual Nutella for mah girls, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3068554-ebony" rel="nofollow noopener"><br>Ebony</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8282085-lisbeth-domus-libri-avery" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisbeth</a> as a sign of gratitute. Without their gushing reviews, I wouldn't go about requesting this from Netgalley.<br><br>I think I may have found my favourite book of 2012 so far.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381327i/738557.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>No, I'm not kitten you. <br><br>My favourite shelf had been so loneleyh! SO LONELEYH! No books, and I mean no books had ever made it into that list after Daughter of Smoke and Bone earlier this year. Some made it close, but this book just went cruuuuuuuuising into my favourite shelf.<br><br>Like a boss.<br><br>This is the book which I need it in physical form no matter what.<br>This is the book which worth a place next to my Lord of the Rings trilogy on my shelf.<br>This is the book which needs to be read slowly because you don't want it to end.<br>This is the book which I'll re-read over and over again in my lifetime until the cover eventually falls off.<br>This is the book I want to marry. I don't care if I die alone with 72 cats.<br>This is the book which left me lost for words. I have nothing bad to say about it! Now, how the hell I'm going to write a review if I like everything about this book?<br><br>I know, I know...shame on me for never running out of ideas on how to condemn a book but not to praise it.<br><br>I mean, I expect nothing less from an author with mitochondrial as her twitter username.<br><br>This is a usual story of how a girl meets a boy, well, except that the girl is Ananna, a pirate and the boy is Naji, a blood magician/assassin who is assigned to kill Ananna. Ananna is hunted by the groom's family when she decided to escape the wedding day. During the confrontation between Naji and Ananna, Ananna accidentally saved Naji's life which resulting in an impossible curse inflicted onto Naji. Consequently, Naji is bound to be with Ananna all the time to protect her, otherwise he will experience great physical pain. Together they cross the desert, the ocean and a magical island on a mission to break the curse.<br><br>Hurm, that's why I hate summarizing. The story ended up sounding so dry.<br><br>It was hard to get into at first for me. First, because it's from Ananna POV and she got all these pirates vibes going on in her speech and monologues. Second, I couldn't grasp the reality of her relationship with her parents that made her decided, it's okay to leave them to escape the arranged marriage. <br><br><b>Ananna</b> or as I'd like to call her<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381327i/738558.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>How do I describe this young lady... I adore her so much, I wish to breed her, I wish for all the versions of myself in parallel universe to be like her. She is err...Anannananana batman. Unique. Fearless but not reckless. Ambitious but practical. Eager to learn. She does all those pirate stuff, cursing, shoplifting, pickpocketing but she possesses an admirable ability for compassion and loyalty. She could just leave Naji to die in the desert but she sticks with him anyway, through thick and thin.<br><br>Most importantly, she is so much fun to read, to learn about.<br><br><i>I was building up to my best one, about a whore and a court magician, and I knew it'd get a laugh of Naji for sure.<br><br>I like 'em well enough, even though they teased me and tried to embarrasses me with crude stories and the like. Course, I had a few stories up my sleeve that made them blush.<br><br>He was curled up on the net and didn't move. "E'mko and his twelve dancing seahorses, you better not be dead."<br><br>A million possibilities raced through my head. Maybe he'd turned into moonlight after all, and I was next. Maybe he'd turned into a fern and I was ripping him into shreads in my fear.</i><br><br><b>Naji</b><br><br>WANTED: OVARIES DONOR. <br><br>Damn, I lost my ovaries to Logan from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283188990" rel="nofollow noopener">Defiance</a> two days ago but right now I'm in dire need to have them back so that I can explode them all over again. For Naji. <br><br>Not much has been revealed about Naji's background up until this book but I think I've learned enough about him to decide that he is indeed swoonworthy. Naji doesn't talk a lot, hides many things, a bit sarcastic, rarely smiles let alone laughs but he is not a douche, not even close. Instead, he is sort of ermm...socially awkward no matter you believe it or not. He is...well, Naji, a very special character and perfect for Anannananana batman.<br><br><i>"You really don't have to stay-it's-well, I'm doing something very rare, full ack'mora-I wouldn't expect-" He straighened up, ran one hand through his tangled-up hair. "Though I ask that you stay in the hotel. My-oath-I'm not sure what would happen to me if you got caught up in danger while I'm away."</i><br><br>*sigh* Well, I ran out of things to say, so to whom I recommend this book to? I want to say everyone but I don't think this book will appeal to everyone. Not that I care, hah! I'd love this anyway if the whole world hates it. Suffice to say that if you're looking for romance and cookie-cutter male and female protagonists, you wouldn't get any because this is one of those books where the characters started off as friends, taking their time to know each other first. A relationship built on trust not lust.<br><br>So...Book2, The Pirate's Wish<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381327i/738559._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>NOW!!!!<br><br><i>**The ARC was provided by Strange Chemistry in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16269258769958596037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1887770117?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=didn-t-finish">didn-t-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1887770117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5731799313069175895"><b>DNF @26%</b><br/><br/>Pirates? <br/><br/>Assassins? <br/><br/>Sign me up!<br/><br/>...and then quickly un-sign me. Because as fun as this idea is, it’s executed really poorly. <br/><br/>The story focuses on Ananna, who runs away from her pirate family to escape an arranged marriage. In doing so, she invokes the wrath of an assassin, and accidentally binds them together with a curse or some other mumbo-jumbo.<br/><br/>(I’m gonna be honest, I didn’t make it to the curse part.)<br/><br/>Though I really hate to put this down so early, I <i>cannot</i> get into this writing style </span>
  <span id="freeText5731799313069175895" style="display:none"><b>DNF @26%</b><br /><br />Pirates? <br /><br />Assassins? <br /><br />Sign me up!<br /><br />...and then quickly un-sign me. Because as fun as this idea is, it’s executed really poorly. <br /><br />The story focuses on Ananna, who runs away from her pirate family to escape an arranged marriage. In doing so, she invokes the wrath of an assassin, and accidentally binds them together with a curse or some other mumbo-jumbo.<br /><br />(I’m gonna be honest, I didn’t make it to the curse part.)<br /><br />Though I really hate to put this down so early, I <i>cannot</i> get into this writing style where the first-person POV features a very uneducated and colloquial narrative voice. It seriously felt like half the words were "ain't" and the other half were "had." Example:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “I ain’t never liked snakes. You don’t see enough of 'em on the water to get used to ‘em, really, and when I saw this one I shrieked without meaning to and stuck my knife clean through it, cause my fear had turned me into a fool who only acted on reflex.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Besides that, the story gave me <i>no</i> incentive to continue. Ananna runs away from her family without a second thought. There’s <i>no</i> emotional element to any of her actions, and <i>all</i> the descriptions are devoted to making sure she seems spunky and rebellious.<br /> <br />I received this through a book-chain over at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/161636-challenge-corner" rel="nofollow noopener">Challenge Corner,</a> a really fun group with a lot of buddy reads and challenges—much more fun than this book, sadly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5731799313069175895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1110579932" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1110579932" />
    <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter"><img alt="Rachel E. Carter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512593159p2/29482005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1110579932?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel E. Carter" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter">Rachel E. Carter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1110579932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6674195928069441741"><b>Ladies and Gentleman, this is how you do fantasy.</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781259ra/13261463.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If you enjoy spunky, defiant protagonists a la Alanna (Song of the Lioness) or Saba (Blood Red Road), or, hell, even Arya Stark, then meet Ananna: the headstrong pirate’s daughter who wants to own her own ship to pillage the coast one day. <i>Umm, who doesn’t?</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781351ra/13261470.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> If you enjoy awesome world building (and we are talking the desert, sea, and a magicked island –how many times do you get all three settings in one book?) then you need to Buy. This. Now.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381111025ra/4236963.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But w</span>
  <span id="freeText6674195928069441741" style="display:none"><b>Ladies and Gentleman, this is how you do fantasy.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781259ra/13261463.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you enjoy spunky, defiant protagonists a la Alanna (Song of the Lioness) or Saba (Blood Red Road), or, hell, even Arya Stark, then meet Ananna: the headstrong pirate’s daughter who wants to own her own ship to pillage the coast one day. <i>Umm, who doesn’t?</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781351ra/13261470.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> If you enjoy awesome world building (and we are talking the desert, sea, and a magicked island –how many times do you get all three settings in one book?) then you need to Buy. This. Now.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381111025ra/4236963.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But what is the most important reason to read this book? <i>The writing.</i> I can honestly name on one hand the number of authors who I would still devour if they omitted romance from their books. <s>And I am a total romance whore.</s> For me usually the best part of a book is the tension between the main character &amp; her love interest -and I tend to spend most of my time counting down until the next scene between whatever character I am shipping, but occasionally I find myself so wrapped up in the author’s unique style that the romance just becomes just a pleasant side effect. Think about Harry Potter. There was no romance for the first couple of books, and yet while I was totally rooting for Ron &amp; Hermoine, they weren’t the main reason I read them. But, let’s admit, it’s awesome that this happened:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781259ra/13261464.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, yeah, Ananna &amp; Naji? Of course I want them to be together. This was pretty much going through my mind during all their scenes:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781351ra/13261471.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Followed by this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781259ra/13261466.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am human after all, and poor Ananna deserves a break. Did Naji stand out as one of my favorite love interests of all time? No. Did I hate him? Absolutely not. Was there instalove? Hell no. Would I reread this as a standalone if I never got closure <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[or even a kiss <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? Yes. And that makes this book stand out.<br><br>Will I be reading the sequel? It’s already on my e-reader. <i>You bet I will.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_481242856" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481242856" />
    <a title="Ava" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5832186-ava"><img alt="Ava" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481242856?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ava" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ava" href="/user/show/5832186-ava">Ava</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=paper-copy">paper-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=paranormal-romance-fiction">paranormal-romance-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=dat-title">dat-title</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=two-stars">two-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481242856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14691204542509750660">I don't think there are words to describe my severe disappointment after finishing THE ASSASSIN'S CURSE.<br/><br/>I began the book with high expectations after individually going through the glowing reviews my <s>co-blogger</s> friends wrote. I was ridiculously excited for THE ASSASSIN'S CURSE - but not only did it let me down... I disliked it heartily in general.<br/><br/>I, along with a majority of the readers, found the idea of the plot to be interesting and original - a strong, independent pirate-chick on a quest to c</span>
  <span id="freeText14691204542509750660" style="display:none">I don't think there are words to describe my severe disappointment after finishing THE ASSASSIN'S CURSE.<br><br>I began the book with high expectations after individually going through the glowing reviews my <s>co-blogger</s> friends wrote. I was ridiculously excited for THE ASSASSIN'S CURSE - but not only did it let me down... I disliked it heartily in general.<br><br>I, along with a majority of the readers, found the idea of the plot to be interesting and original - a strong, independent pirate-chick on a quest to cut the bond between an assassin and herself. Plus, the blurb promised melting romantic tension, and I adore that in my novels.<br><br><s>It's because I'll be forever alone, so might as well read about other teenagers falling in love, eh?</s><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401402ra/779106.gif" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But I found myself totally unimpressed with the plot, the characters, the writing, and the romance throughout the whole novel - not just the beginning, which was said to be the weakest part.<br><br>The storyline dragged on and on, and I could completely imagine THE ASSASSIN'S CURSE as a prequel novel. Why? The blurb lied, because Ananna and Naji only begin the quest to sever the curse at the very end.<br><br>The world-building was subtle and well-done, but there also weren't enough details. I'm still in the dark about the Empire and the Confederacy, because Clark didn't expand on it enough.<br><br>In case you haven't noticed, Ananna is a pirate. The opening sentence contained the word ain't in it, and from there on, I could barely focus on the story because I was too busy translating her bad grammar and language in general. She didn't even sound like a freaking pirate in my head - she sounded Southern, because, you know, that's the first thing that comes to my mind when someone says <i>ain't</i>.<br><br>I only got a break from it when Naji or another character spoke.<br><br>The writing flowed perfectly with Ananna's thoughts: choppy, simple, and easy to understand, but lacking in elegance, too.<br><br>Nearly every character was flat and two-dimensional - especially Leila, a river nymph who's only purpose was to spite Ananna, sabotage them, and act like a high-school bitch. No one gives a shit about Leila, right? Because there was no point in having such a flat character.<br><br>While various bloggers and reviewers found Ananna to be a hilarious badass, I can barely even express my hatred of her. Annoying, bratty, naive, stupid, and whiny (YOU WANT SOME CHEESE WITH THAT WHINE, SWEETHEART?), I despised her with a passion. The world revolved around Ananna and her constant complaining about how ugly she was irked the crap out of me. <br><br>Now, Ananna was also very realistic, and a survivalist, and I appreciated that. But when she's throwing quotes like these out, I lost all the remaining respect I had for her:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>She's beautiful. It means she ain't trustworthy... Beautiful people, things are too easy for 'em. They don't know how to survive in this world. Somebody's ugly, or even plain, normal-looking, that means they got to work twice as hard for things. For anything. Just to get people to listen to 'em, or take 'em serious. So yeah. I don't trust beautiful people.</i>
  <br>
</blockquote><br>First of all, Miss Pineapple (yes, her name means pineapple in French), you ungrateful little girl, 'beautiful people don't know how to survive in this world'? That's the most ignorant thing I've read this year. And I don't think life is going to be any easier for, let's say, a model gang-raped and murdered. Because in the end, if you're dead, and the model is dead, you're BOTH FUCKING SIX FEET UNDER, AREN'T YOU?<br><br>Don't trust good-looking people, guys, because they'll all stab you in the back.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401402ra/779107.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't stand heroines without a backbone: heroines who need the guy to always save them, heroines who can't stand up for themselves. Heroines who have absolutely no confidence in themselves, and most of all, I can't stand damsels in distress.<br><br>Hi, I'd like to introduce you to Naji.<br><br>Please meet the weakest, blindest, most sensitive, mysterious, and unconfident hero in young-adult literature I have read to date.<br><br>Just because you're a guy doesn't mean you get a free pass on this bullshit, because I am not sexist, believe it or not. Having a hero who looks at themselves in the mirror and goes 'boo-whoo-whoo, I'm so fugly', is just as frustrating as having a heroine who does it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401402ra/779108.gif" width="370" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would literally not be surprised if Naji looked at himself in the mirror and imagined that happening.<br><br>As part of the curse, Naji is supposed to 'protect' Ananna, but it really just ends up as Ananna going all Avatar on his ass. All. The. Time.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380401402i/779109._SX540_.jpg" width="370" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Except that it wasn't scarce, like in Avatar, and it definitely wasn't as sexy as that scene. Sure, Naji had an excuse for being such a damso-in-distress - using magic took up his energy and life force.<br><br>IT'S.<br>STILL.<br>INFURIATING.<br><br>I want a guy who can take care of himself and a girl who can too. Having a girl constantly protect a guy, and vice versa, is <i>equally</i> tiring.<br><br>And there was one area that had me tearing my hair out:<br><br>THE PERSON<br>WHO WROTE<br>THE BLURB<br>IS A<br>TOTAL<br>LIAR.<br>AGAIN.<br><br>There is absolutely no bloody romance in THE ASSASSIN'S CURSE, and sure, I can deal with that. But when I'm told that it's a swooning romance and it's actually a nonexistent, ill-founded, unrequited love, I am going to get annoyed.<br><br>I was promised some damn romance and I was lied to, because there was no chemistry, no kiss, and no attraction at all. I hate insta-love as much as the next person, but this can't even be called slowly falling in love BECAUSE THERE WAS NO EFFING ROMANCE. STOP FEEDING ME BULLSHIT. How about you just tell me that they're friends in this book, and in the next book, tell the truth?<br><br>Literally, the closest thing to 'romance' was their bickering, and it wasn't even good fighting. No romantic undertones, no fun bantering. Nada.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/397559.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>THE ASSASSIN'S CURSE was a serious miss for me. A lot of people adored it, and I'm sad to say that I was not one of them. Perhaps the second book will be better, because I'm fairly certain my co-blogger Lisbeth will murder me if I don't start loving the series.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401402ra/779110.gif" width="370" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14691204542509750660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_337963474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337963474" />
    <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-"><img alt="Jillian -always aspiring-" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393566262p2/3085436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337963474?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian -always aspiring-" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-">Jillian -always aspiring-</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Tamora Pierce and Robin McKinley</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=heroines-i-love-and-or-admire">heroines-i-love-and-or-admire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=wowed-me">wowed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=glad-i-gave-it-a-chance">glad-i-gave-it-a-chance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=heroes-i-love-and-respect">heroes-i-love-and-respect</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=world-building-worth-noting">world-building-worth-noting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=wish-i-could-write-a-book-like-this">wish-i-could-write-a-book-like-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=forewent-sleep-to-read-it">forewent-sleep-to-read-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337963474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1255059223720368040">When I first read the synopsis for Cassandra Rose Clarke's <i>The Assassin's Curse</i>, I was very intrigued. Pirates? Assassins? Magic? Curses? Yes, please! Who wouldn't want to read a novel that seems like what might have happened if someone like Tamora Pierce had written <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i>? As often as I've been burned by false promises in novel synopses, I need not have worried with this novel:  <i>The Assassin's Curse</i> fulfilled its promises and managed to soar above and beyond my expectations.<br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText1255059223720368040" style="display:none">When I first read the synopsis for Cassandra Rose Clarke's <i>The Assassin's Curse</i>, I was very intrigued. Pirates? Assassins? Magic? Curses? Yes, please! Who wouldn't want to read a novel that seems like what might have happened if someone like Tamora Pierce had written <i>Pirates of the Caribbean</i>? As often as I've been burned by false promises in novel synopses, I need not have worried with this novel:  <i>The Assassin's Curse</i> fulfilled its promises and managed to soar above and beyond my expectations.<br /><br />In a world where a Pirate's Confederation rules the seas and assassins stalk the shadows, Ananna of the Tanarau finds herself in a precarious position: she is engaged to marry Tarrin, son of the Hariri, yet she has no plans to play wife to a pirate captain's son. Rather, she wants to <i>be</i> the pirate captain, leading her own ship and crew. Even though Tarrin promises that his family will send an assassin after her if she were to leave, Ananna takes her chance and escapes her arranged marriage...but her goals are put on hold when she finds herself faced with the assassin hired by the Hariri. Through a series of magical mishaps, the unthinkable happens: pirate princess and assassin end up journeying to find a way to break a curse that binds them together. What good can come of these happenings?<br /><br />The first thing that really struck me about this novel was how subtle yet <i>fascinating</i> the world-building was. For one, I don't think I've read a novel recently that managed to contain so many culture cues and nods without being overwrought or feeling too authorially maneuvered for diversity's sake. Here everything felt <i>natural</i>, even with the shadow-traveling assassins (who reminded me of ninjas at times) and blood magic and mentions of mystical creatures. It was one of those worlds I never wanted to leave because it seemed so full of possibility.<br /><br />Of course, Ananna herself really stole my attention. Recently, I've found myself really admiring narratives that manage to capture a character's specific voice (Moira Young's <i>Blood Red Road</i> and A.C. Gaughen's <i>Scarlet</i> come to mind), and I can add <i>The Assassin's Curse</i> to the list because this novel also bears quite a distinctive voice in Ananna. Beyond that, though, she's the kind of heroine who's really fun to follow because <i>she does things</i>. Ananna doesn't wait for people to do things for her or protect her (instead, she's usually very opposed to these things because she was raised to take care of herself in dangerous situations), and she's a whole spectrum away from <i>passive</i>.<br /><br />With the assassin/would-be hero, Naji, there was quite a role reversal. In some ways, I think he actually took on some of the characteristics usually attributed to YA heroines (mind, I thought this was a *very good* thing). Despite being a capable assassin, Naji  mucks things up quite a bit through some impulsive decisions over the course of the novel and, even with his magic, he's far from "invincible." (Rather, he often ends up drained due to his magic use, leaving Ananna in a bind to drag him to safety somehow.) It's also quite interesting that Naji seems to bear quite a bit of insecurity, all born from people and happenings in his past. Too often in YA novels I see the insecure "I'll never believe I'm beautiful"/"I'm too ugly to be loved" heroines, so it was very refreshing to read about a hero who, despite capability and intelligence, seems to think very little of himself on a person-to-person level. Usually in various media (not just YA novels) we see male characters who are confident, most oftentimes bordering on arrogant, yet rarely do we ever see the ones who bear self-esteem issues and quite a bit of uncertainty. In that respect, Naji seemed very "real" to me as a character, especially in how he acted and interacted with others.<br /><br />Though the novel undoubtedly had flaws, I'm probably too close to it right now as far as "book infatuation" to point them out and note them in this review. The ending came far too abruptly for my liking, though that's likely due to the fact that I really, <i>really</i> wanted a resolution...only to reach the end and think, "Nononono, don't end, don't end... Oh, crap, now I have to wait for the sequel." (Don't we all hate when that happens?) I guess my reaction only gives more testament to how much I really enjoyed this novel and how much I look forward to the sequel, <i>The Pirate's Wish</i>.<br /><br />Needless to say, I feel that <i>The Assassin's Curse</i> is definitely a notable addition to YA fantasy and one that I hope fantasy fans will flock to read and devour come October. It's a fun novel that should quench any reader's thirst for magic, pirates, assassins, and a world where the possible and impossible twine together. Here's hoping that Ananna and Naji's journey will enchant other readers as much as it did me.<br /><br /><i>Note: I received an advanced copy of this book from the publisher through NetGalley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1255059223720368040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2313764203" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313764203" />
    <a title="Ronak Gajjar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70806774-ronak-gajjar"><img alt="Ronak Gajjar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525528784p2/70806774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313764203?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronak Gajjar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronak Gajjar" href="/user/show/70806774-ronak-gajjar">Ronak Gajjar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70806774-ronak-gajjar?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313764203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9187992826310843364"><b>Magic</b> - Check! <br/><b>Pirates</b> - Check!<br/><b>Assassins</b> - Check!<br/><b>The Hero with worst past</b> - Check!<br/><b>The dumbest Heroine who for once doesn’t do what she is told to</b> - Check!<br/><b>Guns</b> - Check!<br/><b>Swords</b> - Check!   <span id="freeText9187992826310843364" style="display:none"><b>Magic</b> - Check! <br><b>Pirates</b> - Check!<br><b>Assassins</b> - Check!<br><b>The Hero with worst past</b> - Check!<br><b>The dumbest Heroine who for once doesn’t do what she is told to</b> - Check!<br><b>Guns</b> - Check!<br><b>Swords</b> - Check! Ah, I know! <br>*Shouts* Even the magic written here was boring! Nothing happening at all like all the times and our female protagonist - <b>Ms.Ananna</b> is so dickhead to even think for once. God knows why how many times <i>she chilled to her bones?</i><br>The only reason that held me or I suppose my lifeline for this book was the <b>Assassin Naji</b>. <br><br>P.S.: I am sure an idiot to continue this series but I cannot stop a series in midway! I am ready for some more torture where I will keep on picturing the dumbass heroine as a pineapple!</span>

<div id="review_347350988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/347350988" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/347350988?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=high-seas-adventures">high-seas-adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer347350988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6820990589362669524">Do you love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9565548.Grave_Mercy__His_Fair_Assassin___1_' title='Grave Mercy (His Fair Assassin, #1) by R.L. LaFevers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Grave Mercy</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9917938.Blood_Red_Road__Dust_Lands___1_' title='Blood Red Road (Dust Lands, #1) by Moira Young' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blood Red Road</a>, or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/41931-bloody-jack' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bloody Jack series</a>? <b>Then you need to read this book</b>.<br/><br/>Do you like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9565548.Grave_Mercy__His_Fair_Assassin___1_' title='Grave Mercy (His Fair Assassin, #1) by R.L. LaFevers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Grave Mercy</a>, but wish it had more actual murder and a less prim heroine?<br/>Do you like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9917938.Blood_Red_Road__Dust_Lands___1_' title='Blood Red Road (Dust Lands, #1) by Moira Young' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blood Red Road</a> but wish it had a plot that actually made sense?<br/>Do you like Jacky Faber, but wish she would just grow up already?<br/><br/><b>Then you <i>definitely</i> need to read this book</b>.<br/><br/>This book is an absolutely entertaining, fun ride that swept me up onto the back of a stolen camel and never let me go. I finished it</span>
  <span id="freeText6820990589362669524" style="display:none">Do you love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9565548.Grave_Mercy__His_Fair_Assassin___1_" title="Grave Mercy (His Fair Assassin, #1) by R.L. LaFevers" rel="nofollow noopener">Grave Mercy</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9917938.Blood_Red_Road__Dust_Lands___1_" title="Blood Red Road (Dust Lands, #1) by Moira Young" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Red Road</a>, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41931-bloody-jack" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bloody Jack series</a>? <b>Then you need to read this book</b>.<br /><br />Do you like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9565548.Grave_Mercy__His_Fair_Assassin___1_" title="Grave Mercy (His Fair Assassin, #1) by R.L. LaFevers" rel="nofollow noopener">Grave Mercy</a>, but wish it had more actual murder and a less prim heroine?<br />Do you like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9917938.Blood_Red_Road__Dust_Lands___1_" title="Blood Red Road (Dust Lands, #1) by Moira Young" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Red Road</a> but wish it had a plot that actually made sense?<br />Do you like Jacky Faber, but wish she would just grow up already?<br /><br /><b>Then you <i>definitely</i> need to read this book</b>.<br /><br />This book is an absolutely entertaining, fun ride that swept me up onto the back of a stolen camel and never let me go. I finished it in one day and it was one of those completely pleasurable, huge-grin-on-my-face reading experiences. <br /><br />I almost didn’t request this book, because I’ve been disappointed so many times by “this type of book.” You know what I mean – fun, romantic adventure stories that inevitably have idiotic love interests or wimpy/spineless heroines, unbelievable happily ever afters, or all the other things that have prejudiced me against reading romance over the years. Or else they’re fun, romantic fantasy stories with black villains and shallow world-building. Thankfully, I am able to accidentally move past my own stupidity every once in a while and give one of “these books” a chance. And every once in a while, I am very pleasantly surprised.<br /><br />I actually requested this for a very random reason: the author’s name is weirdly close to the name I was born with and had for the first 24 years of my life. Plus, there’s just something about girl pirates that will always pique my interest. This book did not disappoint. Ananna is smart, tough, practical, and resourceful. She’s no shrinking violet, although she is realistically young in a few hilarious ways. She's not a gorgeous knock-out who thinks she's plain. She actually spends the majority of this book in men's clothes. Her voice is a complete delight to read, but more than that - she feels like a real person. <br /><br />Ananna wants nothing more than to be the captain of her own pirate ship and sail off into the sunset. Unfortunately, her parents have other ideas: they've already arranged for her to marry the son of another pirate family. Ananna wants none of it, so she escapes on the day of her betrothal by making use of the thieving and trickery she's been specializing in since toddler-hood. Unfortunately, she doesn’t get far before a powerful Assassin, hired by the jilted groom’s family, tracks her down.<br /><br />Naji, the dark Assassin, mysteriously scarred and covered in magical tattoos, trained in blood magic, is a fantastic love interest. He’s quiet and flawed and willing to let Ananna fight her own battles. He’s no controlling macho-man and he doesn’t instantly fall head over heels for the heroine. Quite the contrary, in fact - he seems to be completely oblivious to her as a woman, which is hilarious. Nevertheless, these two have great chemistry and so obviously complement each other that it’s just delicious waiting for them to figure it out.<br /><br />My one criticism is that this book is so short and there are so many things left to be explained – it feels unfinished. It feels like half of a book. When I got to 95%, 96%, 97%...and realized that this was going to end soon with so much left unexplained and unresolved, I felt a bit…FURIOUS, actually. Damn it, waiting a whole year to have any resolution between these two is probably going to kill me. Don’t read this if, <a href="http://bunburyinthestacks.com/discussion-2/ranty-pants-resolution-or-lack-thereof/" rel="nofollow noopener">like my friend Heidi</a>, you prefer not to be left high and dry.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Heart – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KE5GGMhmo-M&amp;feature=player_embedded" rel="nofollow noopener">What About Love?</a><br /><br />Because sometimes a romancey pop song just feels so right. Seriously Naji…think about it. Don’t you want someone to care about you? (Bahahaha…I can’t even type that without busting out laughing.)<br /><br />Also seen at <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/09/ya-review-the-assassins-curse-by-cassandra-rose-clarke.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6820990589362669524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_347528314" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/347528314" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/347528314?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=epic-or-high-fantasy">epic-or-high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer347528314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15714850245770064887"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Give this at least 3 chapters...<br/><br/>...okay, maybe 4 chapters...<br/><br/>...come to think of it, go with 5, just to be safe...</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>3.5 stars. I can't remember where I got hooked, but it took a short amount of time. <i>But when it happened, I was all in.</i> It was sort of like when I read <i>Graceling</i> and felt like the story didn't really start until Katsa and Po hit the road. That's what happened to me with <i>Assassin's Curse.</i> Things start to pick up when Annabanana (uh...or something like that, her name was sim</span>
  <span id="freeText15714850245770064887" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Give this at least 3 chapters...<br /><br />...okay, maybe 4 chapters...<br /><br />...come to think of it, go with 5, just to be safe...</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />3.5 stars. I can't remember where I got hooked, but it took a short amount of time. <i>But when it happened, I was all in.</i> It was sort of like when I read <i>Graceling</i> and felt like the story didn't really start until Katsa and Po hit the road. That's what happened to me with <i>Assassin's Curse.</i> Things start to pick up when Annabanana (uh...or something like that, her name was similar) gets into a scuffle and saves a MOTHEREFFING ASSASSIN'S LIFE. Yep. The girl saves the bad-ass, scarred assassin. <i>From a snake.</i><br /><br />Hence, the curse. You know the, "oh crap, you saved my life, so now I'm bound to protect you" curse? Which makes this hi-lar-i-ous because he was supposed to off her.<br /><br />But, enough summarizing of the first few chapters (you know me, I'll never spoil anything that happens past the first small section). Let's break down the writing style. This reads like a subtle fantasy. Sure, there's magic and assassins and mystical, far-off lands...but no amount of swashbuckling and faux middle-eastern adventures is hiding the cutesy romance. I honestly expected this book to lean more on the guy-appeal side. Now, this isn't to say that guys can't/won't appreciate the book, but I do think there was quite possibly more swooning and pining than anticipated for an adventurous romp about an assassin being cursed. Although, I can admit to being (just a little bit) girly, so I will never turn down a chance to swoon inside of my head at the mysterious, scarred, bad-ass man.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Scars don't spontaneously emerge overnight, Ananna. They come from somewhere."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />So much of the book was spent on a journey, that I think the story suffered a slight hiccup during some of the time spent 'just surviving.' Don't ask me what I'd change because I couldn't tell you. Maybe I just want my travel time to be wrought with <i>Percy Jackson-eseque</i> adventure. Who knows?<br /><br />There was enough that I did enjoy about <i>Assassin's Curse</i>, so I'll gladly continue with the series.<br /><br /><b>Strong Points :</b><br />~ Unique setting. Bonus points for the fantasy version of a historic middle east, as well as the pirating/high seas adventures.<br />~ Likable characters. Nobody's perfect in this tale.<br />~ Unique magic system.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>And he started to dissolve, turning into shadows like the ones I'd seen the first time he attacked me.<br /><br />The room got darker and darker and his tattoos glowed brighter and brighter.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Weak Points :</b><br />~ No real grip on a language style. Some of the descriptions were lush and fell in line with traditional fantasy storytelling, while other descriptions and speech felt almost crude and post-apocalyptic in nature. The lead female has moments where she speaks like someone out of <i>Blood Red Road.</i> I was taken aback for a second when the word 'bullshit' was thrown in. It's a fantasy world with other forms of words being used for slang; I'm not sure why there would be a modern-day swear word thrown into the mix<br />~ The story seemed to flounder in parts, while we waited for things to happen. When the action happened, it was great. When it wasn't happening, not much else was happening.<br /><br /><b>For me, the strong outweighed the weak, so I will call this book a good time. I'm guessing the next installment will be even better.</b><br /><br /><i>This book was provided from the publisher through Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15714850245770064887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5601896438066038746">A very unusual fantasy, with a female pirate hero and a brooding assassin male hero. You have to know I loved it because I gave it a quote for the cover!</span>
